COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 8: Sales Outsourcing

Recognizing the importance of efficiency and delegation, Chapter 8 explores the benefits of sales outsourcing. It guides readers through identifying tasks in their sales process that are best suited for outsourcing to virtual assistants (VAs), such as lead list building, lead research, data entry, and email outreach.

Key Terms and Definitions

Virtual Assistant (VA): A remote worker who provides administrative, technical, or creative assistance to clients.

Main Concepts

Outsourcing tasks to VAs can free up time for salespeople to focus on higher-value activities.

VAs can handle tasks like list building, lead research, data entry, email outreach, and more.

Supporting Evidence

oDesk and TaskUs are highlighted as platforms for finding and hiring VAs.

A sample job posting for a lead generation VA is provided.

Critical Thinking Questions

What specific tasks in your sales process would be best suited for outsourcing to a VA?

What are the potential challenges and benefits of managing a remote team of VAs?

Discussion Topics

The impact of outsourcing on the sales profession.

Ethical considerations of hiring and managing VAs, including fair wages and working conditions.

Implementation Plan

Practical Application 1: Identify Sales Tasks for Outsourcing

Actionable Task 1.1: List Your Current Sales Activities

Break Down Your Sales Process: Create a detailed list of every activity you do as part of your sales process, from initial lead generation to closing deals.

Categorize Activities: Group your activities into categories, such as:

Lead Generation: Finding and qualifying new leads.

Research: Gathering information on prospects and their companies.

Outreach: Making initial contact with leads through email, phone, or social media.

Data Entry: Inputting data into your CRM or other systems.

Scheduling: Coordinating meetings and calls with prospects.

Follow-Up: Staying in touch with leads and nurturing relationships.

Resources:

Your sales process documentation, brainstorming sessions.

Obstacles and Solutions:

Obstacle: Difficulty breaking down your process - Solution: Review the stages and checklists you created in Chapter 7, online reviews of outsourcing platforms.

Obstacle: Concerns about managing remote workers - Solution: Start with a smaller project to test the waters. Choose a platform that provides tools to help you communicate effectively and monitor progress.

Timeline:

1-2 days

Actionable Task 1.2: Create a Detailed Job Posting

Define the Scope of Work: Clearly outline the specific tasks you want the VA to perform.

Set Expectations: State your requirements for experience, skills, communication, availability, and work style.

Include a Sample Task: To screen candidates, include a small sample task (e.g., finding 5 leads that meet specific criteria).

Example Job Posting (Lead Research VA):

Title: Virtual Assistant - Lead Research

Description: We're looking for a highly organized and detail-oriented virtual assistant to help us with lead research. You will be responsible for gathering information on prospects from their websites, social media profiles, and online publications. You should have strong internet research skills, be proficient in using spreadsheets, and have excellent English communication skills.

Sample Task: Please find 5 companies in the [industry] industry with over 100 employees that are located in [location]. Please provide the company name, website, and LinkedIn profile URL for each company.

Resources:

Job posting templates (available online), your activity list from Task 1.1.

Obstacles and Solutions:

Obstacle: Attracting qualified candidates - Solution: Offer a competitive hourly rate, write a clear and engaging job posting, and highlight the benefits of working for your company.

Timeline:

1-2 days

Actionable Task 1.3: Screen Candidates and Make Your Hire

Review Applications: Carefully review applications and select candidates who meet your requirements.

Conduct Interviews: Interview shortlisted candidates via video call to assess their skills, experience, and communication style.

Check References: Verify references to confirm the candidate's past work experience.

Make an Offer: Offer the job to your chosen candidate and agree on an hourly rate and working hours.

Resources:

Your chosen outsourcing platform's communication tools, video conferencing software.

Obstacles and Solutions:

Obstacle: Finding the right fit - Solution: Be clear about your expectations, ask specific questions during interviews, and trust your gut instinct.

Timeline:

1-2 weeks

Practical Application 2: Manage and Train Your VAs Effectively

Actionable Task 2.1: Create Clear Instructions and Training Materials

Document Processes: Create step-by-step guides for the tasks you're outsourcing.

Provide Examples: Include visual aids (screenshots, videos) and examples to illustrate the desired outcome.

Use Project Management Tools: Utilize project management software (Asana, Trello, etc.) to assign tasks, track progress, and communicate with your VAs.

Resources:

Project management software, screen recording tools, document creation software.

Obstacles and Solutions:

Obstacle: Communication barriers - Solution: Use clear and concise language, provide regular feedback, and be patient with your VAs as they learn your processes.

Timeline:

Ongoing (create training materials as you outsource new tasks).

Actionable Task 2.2: Establish Communication Protocols and Feedback Loops

Set Regular Check-Ins: Schedule weekly or bi-weekly meetings to discuss progress, address questions, and provide feedback.

Use Communication Tools: Choose communication methods that work for both you and your VAs (email, instant messaging, video calls).

Encourage Open Communication: Create an environment where your VAs feel comfortable asking questions and providing feedback.

Resources:

Video conferencing software, instant messaging tools, email.

Obstacles and Solutions:

Obstacle: Time zone differences - Solution: Be mindful of time zones and schedule meetings at times that work for everyone. Use asynchronous communication (email, project management tools) to avoid interrupting your VAs' workflow.

Timeline:

Ongoing

Evaluation Criteria

Task Completion: Are your VAs completing tasks accurately and efficiently?

Time Savings: Are you able to free up your time to focus on higher-value sales activities?

VA Satisfaction: Are your VAs engaged and motivated to do their best work?

Additional Resources

Books: "The 4-Hour Workweek" by Tim Ferriss (a classic on outsourcing and productivity), "Virtual Freedom" by Chris Ducker (a guide to building and managing a virtual team).

Online: Upwork Help Center (help.upwork.com), TaskUs Blog (www.taskus.com/blog).

Outsourcing can be a game-changer for sales productivity. By carefully selecting and managing your VAs, you can create a powerful team that supports your sales efforts and allows you to focus on what you do best. On to the next sales hack!

Stresses the importance of choosing the right CRM for managing leads and tracking customer interactions.

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 9: Customer Relationship Management Software

Key Terms and Definitions

CRM: Customer Relationship Management software is a tool for managing and organizing interactions with customers and prospects.

Main Concepts

Choosing the right CRM is essential for organizing sales data, tracking progress, and managing customer relationships.

Supporting Evidence

The chapter provides an overview of several popular CRM options, including:

PipelineDeals

Close.io

Pipedrive

BaseCRM

RelateIQ

Salesforce

Streak

Critical Thinking Questions

What features are most important for your business when choosing a CRM?

How can CRM data be used to improve sales forecasting and performance analysis?

Discussion Topics

The role of CRM in data-driven sales organizations.

The future of CRM and emerging trends in customer relationship management technology.

Implementation Plan

Practical Application 1: Choose the Right CRM for Your Needs

Actionable Task 1.1: Define Your CRM Requirements

Steps:

Team Size and Structure: Determine how many salespeople will be using the CRM and if there are different teams or roles (e.g., SDRs, AEs, account managers).

Sales Process: Identify the stages of your sales pipeline and whether a customizable CRM is needed.

Features: Consider essential features, including:

Contact Management: Storing and organizing contact information, tracking interactions.

Lead Management: Tracking leads through your pipeline, managing lead scoring.

Deal Management: Tracking deals, managing pipelines, forecasting sales.

Reporting and Analytics: Generating reports on sales performance, tracking metrics.

Email Integration: Syncing emails with the CRM, sending email campaigns.

Mobile Access: Accessing the CRM on smartphones and tablets.

Budget: What is your budget for a CRM?

Integrations: What other tools do you need to integrate with your CRM (e.g., email marketing, marketing automation, calendar)?

Resources: Your sales process documentation and input from your sales team.

Obstacles and Solutions

Obstacle: Difficulty prioritizing features.

Solution: Focus on critical features for your current sales process and team. Start with a simpler CRM and upgrade as needed.

Timeline: 1-2 days.

Actionable Task 1.2: Research and Compare CRM Options

Steps: Explore various CRM options:

PipelineDeals: Simple and easy to use, great for startups and small businesses.

Close.io: Strong focus on sales communication and automation, includes built-in VoIP calling.

Pipedrive: Known for visual pipeline management and ease of use.

BaseCRM: Flexible and affordable with a focus on sales activity tracking.

RelateIQ: Strong in relationship intelligence and uses AI for insights (acquired by Salesforce).

Salesforce: Highly customizable and scalable but can be complex and expensive for startups.

Streak: Simple CRM integrated within your Gmail inbox.

Consider other options: Explore additional CRMs based on your specific industry or needs (e.g., Zoho, HubSpot CRM, SugarCRM).

Resources: Online CRM reviews and comparison websites, free trial offers from CRM providers.

Obstacles and Solutions

Obstacle: Overwhelmed by choices.

Solution: Narrow down options based on defined requirements and prioritize essential features.

Timeline: 1-2 weeks (allow time for research, demoing, and trialing your top choices).

Actionable Task 1.3: Select and Implement Your CRM

Steps:

Choose Your CRM based on research and trials.

Import your existing lead and customer data into your new CRM.

Customize the CRM to match your sales process, including pipeline stages and user permissions.

Train your sales team on effective CRM usage.

Resources: Your chosen CRM, existing data, CRM provider's support documentation.

Obstacles and Solutions

Obstacle: Resistance to adoption from the sales team.

Solution: Communicate benefits clearly and provide ongoing support for a smooth transition.

Timeline: 2-4 weeks (allow time for implementation, customization, and training).

Practical Application 2: Use Your CRM to Manage Your Sales Process

Actionable Task 2.1: Track Leads and Deals

Steps:

Add new leads into your CRM with all relevant information.

Update lead status in the CRM and log interactions as they progress.

Create a deal record in your CRM once a lead qualifies.

Resources: Your CRM and sales process documentation.

Obstacles and Solutions

Obstacle: Inconsistent usage by the sales team.

Solution: Make CRM usage mandatory and integrate it with email and calendar.

Timeline: Ongoing.

Actionable Task 2.2: Leverage Reporting and Analytics

Steps:

Define key metrics to track.

Create custom reports using your CRM's reporting features.

Regularly review reports to identify trends and areas for improvement.

Resources: Your CRM's reporting features and sales goals.

Obstacles and Solutions

Obstacle: Difficulty understanding CRM reports.

Solution: Consult documentation or attend training on reporting features.

Timeline: Ongoing (schedule regular reporting reviews).

Evaluation Criteria

CRM Adoption: Is your sales team using the CRM consistently and effectively?

Data Accuracy: Is your CRM data accurate and up-to-date?

Sales Performance: Are improvements in sales metrics seen as a result of using the CRM?

Additional Resources

Books:

"The Sales Magnet" by Kendra Lee

"Salesforce.com For Dummies" by Tom Wong (if using Salesforce).

Online: Your CRM provider's blog, Sales Hacker blog ( www.saleshacker.com ), HubSpot Sales Blog ( blog.hubspot.com/sales ).

Your CRM is a powerful tool for organizing your sales efforts, tracking your progress, and making data-driven decisions. Embrace its power, and you'll be well on your way to sales success!

Chapter 10: Nurturing Leads and Sparking Engagement

Discusses strategies for lead nurturing and maintaining engagement until prospects are ready to buy.

Sales EQ Chapter 1: The Mysterious Brown Bag - Understanding the Buyer

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

Home

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 1: The Mysterious Brown Bag - Understanding the Buyer

This chapter sets the stage by introducing the concept of Sales EQ and its importance in modern selling. Through the story of "The Mysterious Brown Bag," Blount illustrates how understanding a buyer's perspective, motivations, and language trumps generic pitches. He highlights the power of emotional connection and noncomplementary responses in disrupting buyer scripts and creating differentiation. The chapter emphasizes that people buy for their reasons, not yours, setting the foundation for the book's core principles.

Key Concept

People buy for their reasons, not yours. Successful selling requires understanding the prospect's perspective, motivations, and language.

Practical Application 1: Identifying Buyer Motivations

Actionable Task 1.1: Research and Prep

Steps: Before meeting a prospect, research their company, industry, and role. Look for news articles, blog posts, or LinkedIn profiles to gain insights into their goals, challenges, and language.

Resources: LinkedIn, industry publications, company websites, Google search.

Obstacles/Solutions: Limited information available? Focus on broader industry trends and common challenges for their role.

Timeline: Complete before each initial prospect meeting.

Actionable Task 1.2: Ask, Don't Tell

Steps: During your meeting, use open-ended questions to encourage the prospect to talk about their priorities, concerns, and desired outcomes.

Resources: Prepare a list of insightful questions tailored to their industry/role.

Obstacles/Solutions: Prospect is hesitant to open up? Start with easier, less personal questions and build rapport.

Timeline: Throughout the discovery phase of your sales process.

Evaluation

Success is measured by your ability to articulate the prospect's needs and motivations in their own words, demonstrating a genuine understanding of their perspective.

Additional Resources:

"SPIN Selling" by Neil Rackham (book)

Articles on active listening and effective questioning

Main Concepts

Mastering emotions and interpersonal skills is crucial for UHPs. This involves understanding human psychology and influence frameworks.

Noncomplementary responses can disrupt buyer scripts and shift the power dynamic.

Emotions drive buying decisions, followed by logical justification.

Supporting Evidence

The Mysterious Brown Bag story: Joe, the sales manager, successfully closed a deal by appealing to the bakery owner's emotional connection to his product (bread) and using his language. Average salespeople conform to buyer scripts, leading to lower win probabilities. Joe, the UHP, flipped the buyer script and shaped the decision process.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions:

How can you identify a prospect's underlying motivations and tailor your message accordingly?

What are some noncomplementary responses you can use to disrupt common buyer scripts?

How can you leverage emotional triggers to connect with prospects and influence their decisions?

Supporting Points

Building rapport and understanding the prospect's perspective is essential for building trust.

By addressing the prospect's emotional needs, salespeople can increase their likelihood of closing a deal.

Understanding and leveraging human psychology can give salespeople a significant advantage over their competitors.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that focusing on emotions is manipulative and unethical in sales.

Logic and data should be the primary drivers of complex buying decisions.

Building relationships can distract salespeople from the ultimate goal of closing deals.

Rebuttals

Appealing to emotions is not inherently manipulative. It's about understanding human behavior and building genuine connections.

While logic and data are important, emotions ultimately drive human decisions, even in complex situations.

Building strong relationships is crucial for long-term success and repeat business.

Discussion Topics

The ethical considerations of using emotional intelligence in sales.

The role of data and logic in complex buying decisions.

The balance between building relationships and closing deals.

Chapter 2: A Perfect Sales Storm

Blount paints a picture of the challenging sales landscape characterized by informed buyers and disruptive technology, emphasizing the need to adapt and build authentic relationships.

Sales EQ Chapter 10: Sales Drive - The Fuel of Success

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

Home

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 10: Sales Drive - The Fuel of Success

Blount dives into the concept of Sales Drive - the combination of optimism, competitiveness, and a need for achievement that fuels high performance. He emphasizes the importance of cultivating a positive mindset, embracing challenges, and developing mental toughness. The chapter also explores the impact of physical fitness, sleep, and diet on maintaining high energy levels and emotional control.

Key Terms and Definitions

Sales Drive: A combination of optimism, competitiveness, and a strong need for achievement that fuels ultra-high sales performance.

Optimism: A positive outlook and belief in your ability to succeed, even in the face of challenges.

Competitiveness: A strong desire to win and outperform others.

Need for Achievement: A drive to accomplish challenging goals and strive for excellence.

Internal Locus of Control: A belief that you have control over your own destiny and outcomes.

Main Concepts

Sales Drive is a critical component of Sales EQ and a key differentiator for ultra-high performers (UHPs).

It involves developing and maintaining a positive mindset, embracing challenges, and striving for continuous improvement.

Cultivating Sales Drive requires building an internal locus of control, managing disruptive emotions, and focusing on what you can control.

Supporting Evidence

The research by Dr. Chris Croner highlights that ultra-high performers consistently demonstrate a strong drive to succeed.

The importance of physical fitness and mental toughness emphasizes that peak performance requires both physical and mental resilience.

The impact of sleep and diet on energy levels and emotional control demonstrates how lifestyle choices can significantly affect sales drive.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

How can you develop and maintain a strong Sales Drive, even in challenging sales environments?

What are some strategies for cultivating optimism, competitiveness, and a need for achievement?

How can you manage disruptive emotions and negative self-talk to stay focused and motivated?

Supporting Points

Setting clear goals, visualizing success, and surrounding yourself with positive and supportive people can help you build and maintain Sales Drive.

Embracing competition as a motivator and focusing on continuous learning and self-improvement can enhance your drive to achieve.

Developing a routine of physical exercise, healthy eating, and sufficient sleep can improve your energy levels, mental clarity, and emotional resilience.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that Sales Drive is an inherent trait that cannot be developed.

Excessive competitiveness can lead to unhealthy work habits and burnout.

Focusing on achieving goals might neglect the importance of building relationships and delivering value.

Rebuttals

While some individuals might have a natural inclination toward high drive, it's a quality that can be cultivated and strengthened with effort and intention.

Healthy competition can be a powerful motivator, but it's essential to maintain a balanced approach and avoid overwork and burnout.

Achieving sales goals and building strong relationships are not mutually exclusive. By focusing on delivering value and creating win-win solutions, salespeople can achieve both objectives.

Discussion Topics

The role of passion and purpose in driving sales performance.

The ethical considerations of using competitiveness and a need for achievement in sales.

The importance of work-life balance and self-care for maintaining Sales Drive.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

Sales Drive is the fuel that propels salespeople to overcome challenges, persevere through setbacks, and achieve extraordinary results.

By embracing a growth mindset and focusing on continuous improvement, salespeople can continuously elevate their performance and reach new heights.

Sales Drive is contagious and can inspire both individuals and teams to strive for excellence and create a culture of high achievement.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that Sales Drive can lead to overly aggressive or pushy sales tactics.

Excessive focus on achieving goals can create a stressful and unsustainable work environment.

Sales Drive might not be a suitable quality for all sales roles or personalities.

Rebuttals

Sales Drive should be channeled ethically and focused on creating value for the customer, not just closing deals.

A healthy work environment should balance drive with collaboration, support, and a focus on well-being.

While Sales Drive might be more essential in certain sales roles, it's a valuable quality that can benefit salespeople across all industries and levels of experience.

Practical Application 1: Cultivating Optimism

Actionable Task 10.1: Reframe Negative Self-Talk

Steps: Become aware of your internal dialogue. When you catch yourself engaging in negative self-talk, challenge those thoughts and reframe them in a more positive and constructive way.

Resources: Cognitive behavioral therapy (CBT) techniques, mindfulness exercises, affirmations.

Obstacles/Solutions: Struggling to reframe negative thoughts? Practice replacing each negative thought with three positive ones.

Timeline: Ongoing, as part of your daily routine.

Actionable Task 10.2: Surround Yourself with Positivity

Steps: Spend time with people who are optimistic, supportive, and encouraging. Limit your exposure to negativity, whether it's from news, social media, or toxic individuals.

Resources: Identify positive role models, join supportive communities, or seek out motivational content.

Obstacles/Solutions: Feeling stuck in a negative environment? Actively seek out positive influences and limit your exposure to negativity as much as possible.

Timeline: Make a conscious effort to cultivate a more positive environment both at work and in your personal life.

Evaluation

Success is measured by an increase in your optimism, a reduction in negative self-talk, and a more positive and resilient outlook on challenges and setbacks.

Additional Resources

"Learned Optimism" by Martin Seligman (book)

Articles and resources on optimism, resilience, and positive psychology.

Chapter 11: Self-Control

This chapter discusses the significance of self-control in managing emotions and making constructive decisions during high-stress sales situations.

Sales EQ Chapter 11: Self-Control - Mastering Your Emotions

Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 11: Self-Control - Mastering Your Emotions

This chapter focuses on the importance of managing disruptive emotions that can sabotage sales success. Blount explains the fight-or-flight response and how it triggers emotional reactivity, leading to poor decisions and damaged relationships. He provides practical strategies for developing self-control, including identifying emotional triggers, practicing mindfulness, using the "Push Pause" technique, and consciously choosing your behaviors.

Key Concept

Self-control is crucial for managing disruptive emotions, making rational decisions, and maintaining a professional demeanor, especially in challenging situations.

Key Terms and Definitions

Self-Control: The ability to manage and regulate your emotions and behaviors, especially in challenging or stressful situations.

Disruptive Emotions: Feelings that hijack your rational thinking, cloud your judgment, and lead to unproductive behaviors.

Fight-or-Flight Response: A physiological and psychological reaction to perceived threats, triggering a surge of adrenaline and a shift in focus toward survival.

Cognitive Biases: Systematic errors in thinking that arise from the way our brains process information.

Dual Process: The ability to balance the focus on building relationships and achieving sales objectives while managing disruptive emotions.

Main Concepts

Self-control is a critical component of Sales EQ and essential for navigating the emotional rollercoaster of sales.

Disruptive emotions, often triggered by the fight-or-flight response, can derail sales conversations and sabotage deals.

Developing self-control requires understanding your emotional triggers, practicing mindfulness, and utilizing strategies to regulate your emotional responses.

Supporting Evidence

The example of Shannon losing a deal due to her emotional outburst illustrates how a lack of self-control can damage relationships and sabotage sales opportunities.

The explanation of the fight-or-flight response highlights how our brains and bodies react to perceived threats, leading to disruptive emotions and behaviors.

The concept of "push pause" emphasizes the importance of taking a moment to gather your thoughts and regulate your emotions before reacting to a challenging situation.

Practical Application 1: Utilizing the "Push Pause" Technique

Actionable Task 11.1: Identify Your Emotional Triggers

Steps: Reflect on past situations where you felt overwhelmed by emotions. Identify the specific triggers that caused those reactions, such as certain types of prospects, objections, or pressure situations.

Resources: Journaling, self-reflection exercises, feedback from colleagues who have witnessed your reactions.

Obstacles/Solutions: Difficulty identifying triggers? Pay close attention to your physical and emotional responses during interactions and make note of what sets you off.

Timeline: Ongoing, as you become more self-aware of your emotional patterns.

Actionable Task 11.2: Practice the "Push Pause"

Steps: When you feel a strong emotional reaction, take a deep breath, count to five, and consciously choose a calm and collected response.

Resources: Mindfulness exercises, relaxation techniques, role-playing challenging scenarios with a trusted colleague.

Obstacles/Solutions: Feeling like your emotions are taking over? Excuse yourself from the situation briefly if possible to gather your composure.

Timeline: Practice the "push pause" technique in all your interactions, both professional and personal, to develop greater self-control.

Evaluation

Success is measured by your ability to remain calm and composed in challenging situations, reduce emotional reactivity, and choose responses that are aligned with your values and objectives.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions:

What are some common disruptive emotions that salespeople experience, and how can you manage them effectively?

How can you identify your emotional triggers and develop strategies for regulating your responses?

How can you use self-control to enhance your communication, build stronger relationships, and increase win probability?

Discussion Topics

The importance of emotional regulation in maintaining professionalism and building trust with stakeholders.

The challenges of developing self-control in high-pressure sales environments.

The ethical considerations of using emotional control to influence buyer behavior.

Additional Resources

"The Chimp Paradox" by Steve Peters (book)

Articles and resources on emotional regulation, mindfulness, and stress management.

This continues our "Sales EQ" implementation plan. Stay tuned for the remaining chapters, and remember to tailor these actions to your unique needs and circumstances.

## /blog/sales_eq_chapter_12

Sales EQ Chapter 12: Shaping Win Probability Begins with Qualification

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

Home

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 12: Shaping Win Probability Begins with Qualification

Blount returns to the concept of "win probability" and emphasizes the importance of disciplined qualifying to avoid chasing "ugly deals." He guides readers through the process of defining their "Ideal Qualified Prospect" (IQP) profile, using qualifying frameworks like BANT or MEDDIC, and conducting "murder boarding" to rigorously evaluate opportunities. The chapter underscores the value of investing time wisely in high-probability prospects.

Key Concept

Time is your most valuable asset. Invest it wisely by rigorously qualifying prospects and focusing on those that align with your Ideal Qualified Prospect (IQP) profile.

Key Terms and Definitions

Ideal Qualified Prospect (IQP): A detailed profile that outlines the characteristics of the most promising prospects for a particular product or service.

Strike Zone: The range of prospects that are most likely to buy, based on their alignment with the IQP profile.

Chasing Ugly Deals: Pursuing low-probability prospects that are unlikely to close, often due to disruptive emotions like desperation or attachment.

Main Concepts

Qualifying prospects effectively is crucial for maximizing win probability and minimizing wasted effort.

Developing a clear understanding of your IQP and focusing on prospects within your "strike zone" allows you to be more selective and invest your time wisely.

Chasing "ugly deals" driven by disruptive emotions leads to frustration, wasted resources, and lower sales performance.

Supporting Evidence

The baseball analogy: Demonstrating how swinging at pitches outside the strike zone (chasing ugly deals) rarely leads to success.

The importance of defining your IQP: Highlighting the need for a clear understanding of your ideal customer profile to guide your prospecting and qualifying efforts.

The concept of "murder boarding": Emphasizing the value of rigorously evaluating opportunities to identify potential risks and weaknesses.

Practical Application 1: Defining Your Strike Zone

Actionable Task 12.1: Develop Your IQP Profile

Steps: Outline the specific characteristics of your ideal customers, including industry, company size, revenue, pain points, budget, decision-making process, and stakeholder profiles.

Resources: Analyze your most successful past deals, gather market intelligence, and interview top-performing salespeople in your company.

Obstacles/Solutions: Difficult to define a narrow IQP? Start with broader criteria and refine your profile as you gain more data and experience.

Timeline: Develop your initial IQP profile within the next week. Review and refine it quarterly based on new insights and data.

Actionable Task 12.2: Implement a Qualifying Framework

Steps: Choose a qualifying methodology, such as BANT (Budget, Authority, Need, Timeline) or MEDDIC (Metrics, Economic Buyer, Decision Criteria, Decision Process, Identify Pain, Champion) that aligns with your sales process and IQP.

Resources: Sales EQ training materials, books, and articles on qualifying methodologies.

Obstacles/Solutions: Unsure which framework to choose? Consult with your sales manager or a sales coach to determine the best fit for your situation.

Timeline: Implement your chosen qualifying framework within the next two weeks, and make it a part of your sales process documentation.

Evaluation

Success is measured by a reduction in time spent chasing "ugly deals," an increase in the average deal size and win rate, and a more predictable sales pipeline.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

How can you define your IQP and identify the key characteristics of your most promising prospects?

What are some strategies for effectively qualifying prospects and avoiding "ugly deals"?

How can you use the "murder boarding" technique to improve your decision-making and increase win probability?

Supporting Points

Analyzing past successful deals, gathering market intelligence, and understanding your product or service's value proposition can help you define your IQP.

Asking qualifying questions, listening attentively, and observing nonverbal cues can help you assess a prospect's viability.

Inviting colleagues to challenge your assumptions and play devil's advocate during "murder boarding" can expose potential weaknesses and improve your strategy.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that focusing too narrowly on IQP can limit opportunities and miss out on potentially good prospects that don't fit the profile perfectly.

Excessive qualifying might alienate prospects and make the sales process too rigid.

"Murder boarding" can be too critical and discouraging, leading to a lack of confidence and risk aversion.

Rebuttals

Defining your IQP provides a framework for focusing your efforts on the most promising opportunities, but it should not be a rigid rule that excludes all exceptions.

Effective qualifying is about asking the right questions and listening attentively, not about being interrogative or dismissive.

"Murder boarding" should be done constructively and focus on identifying potential risks and solutions, not on tearing down ideas or demoralizing salespeople.

Discussion Topics

The balance between using IQP as a guide and being open to exploring new possibilities.

The role of intuition and experience in qualifying prospects.

The ethical considerations of using manipulative tactics to "qualify out" prospects that are not a good fit.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

Disciplined qualifying allows salespeople to focus their time and energy on prospects that are most likely to buy, leading to increased efficiency and higher win probability.

By understanding your IQP, you can tailor your sales approach and messaging to resonate with the needs and motivations of your ideal customers.

"Murder boarding" helps identify potential risks and weaknesses early on, allowing you to develop strategies to mitigate them and increase your chances of success.

Counterpoints

Over-qualifying might lead to missed opportunities and a limited customer base.

Focusing too much on IQP might ignore the individual needs and preferences of specific stakeholders.

"Murder boarding" can create a culture of fear and negativity, hindering creativity and innovation.

Rebuttals

Effective qualifying should be balanced with an understanding of the buyer's context and potential for growth. It's about finding the right fit, not about excluding all exceptions.

IQP provides a framework for targeting your ideal customers, but your approach should always be tailored to the individual needs of each stakeholder.

"Murder boarding" should be done constructively, focusing on identifying potential risks and solutions, not on criticizing individuals or ideas. It's about improving, not punishing.

Additional Resources

"The Sales Development Playbook" by Trish Bertuzzi (book)

Articles and resources on qualifying methodologies, lead scoring, and sales pipeline management.

Chapter 13: Engagement and Micro-Commitments

Blount illustrates the importance of gaining small, incremental agreements that build trust and advance deals, nurturing a path toward closure.

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 13: Engagement and Micro-Commitments

This chapter focuses on the importance of securing "micro-commitments" - small, incremental agreements that build momentum and increase buy-in. Blount explains how to test stakeholder engagement, ask for micro-commitments effectively, and leverage the value bias and consistency principle to shape buyer behavior. He emphasizes the need for consistent forward progress and the danger of stalled deals.

Key Terms and Definitions:

Engagement: The level of interest, involvement, and commitment a stakeholder demonstrates during the sales process.

Micro-Commitments: Small, incremental agreements or actions that move a deal forward, building momentum and increasing win probability.

Main Concepts:

Engaging stakeholders and securing micro-commitments are crucial for keeping deals moving forward and preventing stalls.

Testing engagement involves observing emotional cues, asking for small commitments, and being willing to walk away if a stakeholder is not genuinely invested.

Micro-commitments leverage the value bias (people value what they invest in) and the consistency principle (people strive to be consistent with their commitments).

Supporting Evidence:

The story of Kurt Long securing a deal through micro-commitments: Demonstrating how small agreements can build momentum and lead to larger commitments.

The three purposes of testing engagement: Highlighting the importance of assessing stakeholder investment, gauging win probability, and increasing commitment through small steps.

The example of the heavy equipment company and the misinterpreted eagerness: Illustrating how eagerness can be misleading and the importance of testing engagement before assuming a deal is closed.

Critical Thinking Resources:

Critical Thinking Questions:

How can you effectively test engagement and identify whether a stakeholder is genuinely invested in the sales process?

What are some strategies for securing micro-commitments and building momentum towards a close?

How can you leverage the value bias and the consistency principle to influence stakeholder behavior?

Supporting Points:

Asking open-ended questions, observing nonverbal cues, and listening attentively for emotional indicators can help you gauge stakeholder engagement.

Framing requests as small, incremental steps, highlighting the benefits of taking action, and creating a sense of urgency can encourage micro-commitments.

By acknowledging and appreciating each micro-commitment, you reinforce the value bias and encourage the stakeholder to remain consistent with their actions.

Counterpoints:

Some might argue that focusing too much on micro-commitments can make the sales process feel overly transactional and mechanical.

Excessive requests for small commitments might annoy stakeholders and create a sense of pressure.

Relying solely on micro-commitments might neglect the importance of building genuine relationships and understanding the stakeholder's broader needs.

Rebuttals:

Micro-commitments should be used strategically and purposefully, not as a manipulative tactic to pressure buyers. It's about creating a collaborative and transparent sales process.

Framing requests thoughtfully and emphasizing the benefits of taking action can make micro-commitments feel less demanding and more like a natural progression.

Micro-commitments are a valuable tool for building momentum and gauging stakeholder investment, but they should be combined with a genuine focus on building relationships and understanding the buyer's needs.

Discussion Topics:

The balance between focusing on micro-commitments and building authentic relationships.

The role of trust and transparency in securing micro-commitments.

The ethical considerations of using psychological principles to influence stakeholder behavior.

Argument Builder:

Supporting Points:

Securing micro-commitments creates a sense of momentum and makes it progressively harder for stakeholders to back out of a deal.

By consistently testing engagement, salespeople can identify potential roadblocks early on and adjust their approach accordingly.

Micro-commitments leverage psychological principles that are inherent in human decision-making, making them a powerful tool for influencing outcomes.

Counterpoints:

Focusing too much on micro-commitments might neglect the importance of addressing broader stakeholder concerns and building long-term relationships.

Excessive requests for small commitments can make the sales process feel pushy and manipulative.

Stakeholders might perceive micro-commitments as a lack of trust and become resistant to the sales process.

Rebuttals:

Micro-commitments should be part of a holistic sales approach that includes building rapport, understanding needs, and addressing concerns. They are not a replacement for building relationships.

Framing requests thoughtfully, emphasizing the benefits of taking action, and creating a sense of collaboration can make micro-commitments feel less demanding.

Transparency and open communication can help address any concerns stakeholders might have about micro-commitments and build trust in the sales process.

Practical Application 1: Mastering Micro-Commitments

Actionable Task 13.1: Identify Opportunities for Micro-Commitments:

Steps: Review your sales process and identify specific points where you can ask for small commitments, such as agreeing to a next meeting, providing access to data, or introducing you to other stakeholders.

Resources: Sales process documentation, brainstorming sessions with colleagues or a sales coach.

Obstacles/Solutions: Struggling to find opportunities? Get creative and consider any action, no matter how small, that demonstrates progress and buy-in.

Timeline: Identify at least three potential micro-commitments within your sales process by the end of the week.

Actionable Task 13.2: Practice the Assumptive Ask:

Steps: When asking for micro-commitments, use confident and assumptive language, as if you expect the stakeholder to say yes. Avoid hesitant or apologetic phrasing.

Resources: Role-playing with a colleague or sales coach, scripting your assumptive asks in advance.

Obstacles/Solutions: Feeling uncomfortable being assertive? Remind yourself that you are offering value and asking for a reasonable commitment that will benefit the stakeholder.

Timeline: Practice using the assumptive ask in your next three sales conversations.

Evaluation:

Success is measured by an increase in the number of micro-commitments you secure, a reduction in stalled deals, and a more predictable and efficient sales cycle.

Additional Resources:

"The Power of Moments: Why Certain Experiences Have Extraordinary Impact" by Chip Heath and Dan Heath (book)

Articles and resources on persuasion, influence, and commitment techniques.

This chapter addresses the challenge of stalled deals, stressing the necessity of establishing clear next steps to maintain momentum in the sales process.

Chapter 14: Stalled Deals and Next Steps

Blount addresses the common problem of stalled deals and highlights the "Cardinal Rule of Sales Conversations": Never leave a meeting without a firm next step. He explains how to set clear next steps, overcome the fear of asking, and use calendar invites to solidify commitments. The chapter underscores the importance of maintaining momentum and avoiding the "Call Me Maybe" syndrome.

Key Terms and Definitions

Stalled Deals: Opportunities that have lost momentum and are no longer progressing through the sales pipeline.

Next Steps: Clear, specific, and mutually agreed-upon actions that move a deal forward toward the next stage of the sales process.

The Cardinal Rule of Sales Conversations: Never leave a meeting with a stakeholder without setting and committing to a firm next step.

Main Concepts

Stalled deals are a common problem in sales, often caused by a lack of clear next steps and a failure to maintain momentum. Consistently securing micro-commitments and establishing firm next steps is crucial for keeping deals progressing toward a close. Average salespeople often struggle to get firm next steps due to fear of rejection, lack of assertiveness, or a misunderstanding of the buyer's sense of urgency.

Supporting Evidence

The dialogue from a pipeline review illustrates how a lack of clear next steps can lead to stalled deals and a congested pipeline.

The example of Ken, the salesperson who failed to schedule a next appointment, demonstrates the consequences of not securing a firm next step while the opportunity is present.

The Universal Law of Need emphasizes that desperation from an empty pipeline can lead to poor decision-making and lower win probability.

Practical Application 1: Implementing the Cardinal Rule

Actionable Task 14.1: Never Leave a Meeting Without a Next Step

Steps: Before ending any conversation with a stakeholder, ensure you have a clear understanding of the next action to be taken, who is responsible, and when it will be completed.

Resources: Calendar, task management tool, shared document with stakeholders.

Obstacles/Solutions: If a stakeholder is hesitant to commit, offer alternative next steps or adjust the timeline to find a mutually agreeable option.

Timeline: Implement immediately, making it a non-negotiable part of your sales process.

Actionable Task 14.2: Use Calendar Invites to Solidify Commitments

Steps: After agreeing on a next step, send a calendar invitation to the stakeholder to solidify the commitment and ensure it is scheduled.

Resources: Email calendar, scheduling tool.

Obstacles/Solutions: If the stakeholder declines the invite, follow up promptly to understand their concerns and find a workable alternative.

Timeline: Implement for all next steps, making it a standard practice.

Evaluation

Success is measured by a reduction in the number of stalled deals in your pipeline, an increase in deal velocity, and a more accurate sales forecast.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

What are some common reasons why deals stall, and how can you prevent them from happening?

What are the key characteristics of a firm next step, and how can you ensure that you get a commitment from the stakeholder?

How can you overcome the fear of rejection and become more assertive in asking for next steps?

Supporting Points

Clearly defining the next steps, establishing a timeline, and getting agreement from all stakeholders are essential for maintaining momentum.

Framing requests as collaborations and highlighting the benefits of taking action can make it easier for stakeholders to commit to next steps.

Practicing your ask, visualizing success, and remembering that "no" is not a personal attack can help you overcome the fear of rejection.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that being overly assertive in asking for next steps can be off-putting and damage relationships.

Focusing too much on next steps can make the sales process feel rigid and impersonal.

Stakeholders might not always be willing or able to commit to specific next steps, especially in complex deals.

Rebuttals

Assertiveness is not the same as aggressiveness. It's about being clear, confident, and respectful in communicating your expectations.

Next steps should be viewed as guideposts for a collaborative sales process, not as a rigid set of rules.

Flexibility and adaptability are crucial for navigating complex deals, but it's still essential to establish a framework for moving forward and maintain a sense of momentum.

Discussion Topics

The balance between being assertive and being respectful in asking for next steps.

The role of trust and transparency in establishing clear expectations for next steps.

The challenges of managing stakeholder expectations and timelines in complex sales environments.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

Consistently securing firm next steps creates a sense of progress, accountability, and momentum that drives deals toward a close.

By clearly defining expectations for next steps, salespeople can minimize misunderstandings, reduce the risk of stalls, and enhance the overall efficiency of the sales process.

Mastering the art of asking for next steps demonstrates professionalism, confidence, and a commitment to delivering value, ultimately increasing win probability.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that focusing too much on next steps can create unnecessary pressure and urgency, potentially alienating stakeholders.

Stakeholders might perceive a rigid adherence to next steps as a lack of flexibility and a disregard for their individual needs.

The constant need to secure next steps can become a distraction from focusing on building relationships and understanding the bigger picture.

Rebuttals

Next steps should be viewed as milestones in a collaborative journey, not as a means to pressure or rush stakeholders.

Flexibility and adaptability are crucial for navigating complex sales situations, but a clear framework for progress is still essential to maintain momentum and avoid stalls.

Next steps should be integrated seamlessly into the overall sales process, focusing on building relationships, understanding needs, and delivering value while driving progress toward a close.

Additional Resources

"Getting Things Done: The Art of Stress-Free Productivity" by David Allen (book)

Articles and resources on time management, calendar management, and follow-up techniques.

Focusing on the structured sales process, Blount discusses its significance in improving consistency and efficiency in achieving sales goals.

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 15: Sales Process - The Framework for Success

This chapter emphasizes the need for a well-defined and executed sales process. Blount outlines a basic seven-step sales process: Prospecting, Connecting, Discovering, Bridging, Asking, Handling Objections, and Implementing/Account Management. He discusses common reasons why salespeople fail to leverage the sales process effectively, including disruptive emotions, winging it, complexity, and a lack of a defined process.

Key Concept

A well-defined sales process provides a roadmap for consistent execution, minimizes mistakes, and increases win probability.

Key Terms and Definitions

Sales Process: A systematic and repeatable set of steps that salespeople follow to guide prospects through the buying journey, from initial contact to close.

Main Concepts

A well-defined sales process is essential for creating consistency, improving efficiency, and increasing win probability.

The sales process provides a framework for managing interactions with stakeholders, aligning activities with buyer behavior, and driving progress toward a close.

Salespeople often fail to execute the sales process effectively due to disruptive emotions, a lack of discipline, or an overly complex or nonexistent process.

Supporting Evidence

Jeffrey Gitomer's quote: "Sales is a process - a completely predictable process. Follow the steps and you close deals. Skip steps and you lose."

The four reasons why salespeople fail to leverage the sales process: Impact of disruptive emotions, winging it, complexity, and lack of a defined process.

The basic seven-step sales process: A fundamental framework for guiding stakeholders through the buying journey, regardless of industry or product.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

What are the key benefits of having a well-defined sales process, and how can it improve your sales performance?

What are some common mistakes salespeople make when executing the sales process, and how can you avoid them?

How can you adapt the basic seven-step sales process to fit your specific industry, product, and target market?

Supporting Points

A clearly defined sales process helps salespeople stay organized, manage their time effectively, and maintain a consistent approach, leading to improved efficiency and higher win probability.

By aligning your sales process with the buyer's journey, you can create a smoother and more positive customer experience, enhancing engagement and building trust.

Regularly evaluating and refining your sales process based on feedback, data, and industry trends ensures that it remains relevant and effective.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that a rigid sales process stifles creativity and prevents salespeople from adapting to individual customer needs.

An overly complex sales process can be overwhelming and cumbersome, hindering action and slowing down the sales cycle.

Salespeople might resist adopting a defined sales process if they perceive it as a threat to their autonomy or a lack of trust in their abilities.

Rebuttals

A well-defined sales process provides a framework for action, not a rigid set of rules. Flexibility and adaptability are still essential for tailoring your approach to individual customer needs.

Complexity should be avoided when designing a sales process. It's important to keep it simple, clear, and actionable, focusing on the essential steps that drive progress.

Adopting a defined sales process should be seen as a collaborative effort to improve efficiency and achieve better results, not as a means to micromanage or control salespeople.

Discussion Topics

The balance between process and flexibility in sales.

The role of technology in automating and streamlining the sales process.

The importance of buy-in and ownership from salespeople when implementing a new sales process.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

A well-defined sales process creates consistency, predictability, and accountability, leading to improved sales performance and a more positive customer experience.

By aligning your sales process with the buyer's journey and leveraging data and insights, you can create a more targeted and effective sales approach.

A robust sales process provides a framework for continuous improvement, allowing you to identify areas for optimization and adapt to changing market conditions.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that a rigid sales process can be a barrier to innovation and prevent salespeople from developing creative solutions.

Overemphasis on process might stifle intuition and experience, leading to a loss of the human element in sales.

Salespeople might perceive a defined sales process as a lack of trust in their judgment and abilities, hindering adoption and buy-in.

Rebuttals

A well-designed sales process should encourage creativity and innovation by providing a framework for testing new ideas and adapting to individual customer needs.

Intuition and experience are essential components of successful selling, and they can be enhanced by a robust sales process that provides insights and data to support decision-making.

Implementing a new sales process should be a collaborative effort, involving input from salespeople and emphasizing the benefits of improved efficiency, higher win probability, and a more positive customer experience.

Practical Application 1: Simplifying and Aligning Your Sales Process

Actionable Task 15.1: Map Your Current Sales Process

Steps: Outline the steps you currently take when selling, from initial contact to close. Be honest about what you actually do, not what you ideally should do.

Resources: Whiteboard, flowcharting software, sales process templates.

Obstacles/Solutions: Your process seems messy or undefined? Don't be afraid to start from scratch and design a process that is simple, clear, and actionable.

Timeline: Complete a visual representation of your current sales process within the next week.

Actionable Task 15.2: Align Your Process with the Buyer's Journey

Steps: Compare your sales process to the typical stages a buyer goes through when making a purchase decision. Identify any gaps or misalignments, and adjust your process accordingly.

Resources: Research on the buyer's journey for your target market, feedback from clients, sales process best practices.

Obstacles/Solutions: Struggling to understand the buyer's journey? Interview recent customers to get their perspective on the steps they took before choosing you.

Timeline: Complete an analysis and alignment of your sales process within the next two weeks.

Evaluation

Success is measured by a more streamlined and effective sales process, greater clarity and consistency in your sales activities, and a reduction in friction or confusion during the sales cycle.

Additional Resources

"The Sales Magnet" by Kendra Lee (book)

Articles and resources on sales process mapping, buyer journey mapping, and sales enablement.

These actionable tasks and implementation strategies will guide you in applying "Sales EQ" to enhance your sales performance. Continue working through the chapters to build a solid foundation for building your Sales EQ!

Understanding the buying process and aligning it with the sales process is essential for increasing win probability and providing a smooth customer experience.

Chapter 16: Buying Process - Aligning for Success

Blount shifts the focus to understanding the buyer's journey and aligning your sales process to their needs and expectations. He cautions against becoming a "buying process puppet" and emphasizes the importance of "shaping the buying process" to gain a competitive advantage. The chapter explores strategies for mapping the buyer's journey, identifying key decision points, and adapting your approach to create a more seamless customer experience.

Key Concept

Understanding the buyer's journey and aligning your sales process to their needs and expectations is crucial for increasing win probability.

Key Terms and Definitions

Buying Process: The series of steps a prospect goes through when making a purchase, from identifying a need to selecting a vendor and implementing a solution.

Main Concepts

Understanding the prospect's buying process is essential for aligning your sales process and increasing win probability.

The buying process can vary significantly depending on the complexity of the sale, the industry, and the individual organization's culture and decision-making style.

Average salespeople often fail to map the buying process, leading to getting out of sync with the prospect's expectations and a decrease in win probability.

Supporting Evidence

The example of the on-site childcare RFP process illustrates how failing to understand the prospect's buying process can lead to wasted resources and lost deals.

The danger of becoming a "buying process puppet," highlighting how salespeople can lose control of the sales process by blindly following the prospect's dictates.

The importance of "shaping the buying process" emphasizes how UHPs influence the buying process to align it with their sales process, giving them a competitive advantage.

Practical Application 1: Mapping the Buyer's Journey

Actionable Task 16.1: Research Your Target Market's Buying Process

Steps: Conduct research to understand the typical steps your target customers take when making a purchase decision in your industry. Consider their motivations, pain points, research methods, and decision criteria.

Resources: Industry reports, buyer persona templates, online forums, competitor analysis, customer interviews.

Obstacles/Solutions: Difficulty finding specific information? Focus on general buying stages (awareness, consideration, decision, implementation) and adapt them to your specific context.

Timeline: Complete your research within one week.

Actionable Task 16.2: Create a Buyer Journey Map

Steps: Visually map out the steps your ideal customer takes, including their thoughts, feelings, and actions at each stage. Identify potential touchpoints where your sales process can align and add value.

Resources: Whiteboard, sticky notes, buyer journey mapping templates.

Obstacles/Solutions: Feeling overwhelmed by complexity? Focus on the key stages and decision points, and keep your map simple and clear.

Timeline: Create your initial buyer journey map within two weeks. Review and refine it quarterly as you gain more insights.

Evaluation

Success is measured by your ability to articulate the buyer's journey in your own words, identify key decision points and influencers, and align your sales activities to the buyer's needs at each stage.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

How can you effectively map the buying process for your prospects, and what questions should you ask to gather this information?

What are some common challenges in understanding and aligning with the buying process, and how can you overcome them?

How can you "shape" the buying process to increase win probability without being manipulative or disrespectful?

Supporting Points

Asking open-ended questions about the prospect's past buying experiences, their decision-making criteria, and their internal approval process can help you map their buying process.

Collaboration, flexibility, and a willingness to adapt your sales process to the prospect's needs can help you stay in sync and maintain momentum.

Offering valuable insights, addressing the prospect's concerns, and demonstrating a genuine understanding of their challenges can influence the buying process without being manipulative.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that attempting to shape the buying process is manipulative and disrespectful of the prospect's autonomy.

The buying process can be complex and fluid, making it difficult to map accurately and align with perfectly.

Focusing too much on the buying process might distract salespeople from the core aspects of selling, such as building relationships and presenting value.

Rebuttals

Shaping the buying process is about adding value and creating a smoother experience for the prospect, not about manipulating them into making a decision.

While the buying process might not be perfectly linear, understanding the key stages and decision points can significantly improve your chances of success.

Mapping the buying process should enhance your selling efforts by providing insights into the prospect's needs, priorities, and decision-making style, allowing you to tailor your approach accordingly.

Discussion Topics

The ethics of influencing the buying process.

The role of technology in shaping and managing the buying process.

The challenges of aligning sales and buying processes in complex sales environments.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

Understanding the buying process allows salespeople to anticipate stakeholder needs, tailor their approach, and present solutions that align with the prospect's priorities.

By shaping the buying process, salespeople can create a more efficient and predictable path to closing, increasing win probability and reducing the risk of stalls.

Aligning the sales process with the buying process enhances the customer experience, leading to stronger relationships and increased customer satisfaction.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that focusing too much on the buying process can make the sales process feel overly structured and impersonal.

Stakeholders might perceive attempts to shape the buying process as a lack of respect for their established procedures.

Overemphasis on process can distract salespeople from the human element of selling and the importance of building genuine connections.

Rebuttals

The buying process should be viewed as a framework for collaboration, not as a rigid set of rules. Flexibility and adaptability are still crucial for tailoring your approach to individual customer needs.

Transparency and open communication can help address any concerns stakeholders might have about your efforts to shape the buying process.

Understanding and aligning with the buying process should enhance your ability to build relationships and deliver value by providing insights into the prospect's needs and priorities.

Additional Resources

Mapping Experiences: A Complete Guide to Customer Journey Mapping by Jim Kalbach (book)

Articles and templates on buyer journey mapping.

Sales EQ Chapter 17: The Five Stakeholders You Meet in a Deal

COLD CALLING THAT CONVERTS

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 17: The Five Stakeholders You Meet in a Deal

This chapter introduces the "BASIC" stakeholder framework: Buyers, Amplifiers, Seekers, Influencers, and Coaches. Blount emphasizes the importance of mapping the stakeholder landscape, understanding their individual motivations, and developing a tailored engagement strategy for each key player. He highlights the power of building a coalition of support and leveraging the influence of amplifiers and coaches.

Key Terms and Definitions

BASIC Stakeholders: The five key roles that individuals typically play in a buying decision:

Buyers: Individuals with the authority to make a purchase decision.

Amplifiers: Individuals who champion your solution and advocate for your company within the organization.

Seekers: Individuals tasked with gathering information and evaluating options.

Influencers: Individuals whose opinions and recommendations carry weight in the decision-making process.

Coaches: Individuals who provide you with insider information, guidance, and support to help you navigate the buying process.

Main Concepts

Understanding the roles and influence of all stakeholders involved in a deal is essential for increasing win probability.

Mapping the stakeholder landscape allows you to identify key players, understand their motivations, and tailor your approach accordingly.

Average salespeople often focus only on identifying the "decision maker," while UHPs take a more comprehensive approach to understanding the entire stakeholder array.

Supporting Evidence

The example of the complex software deal with 22 stakeholders illustrates the importance of understanding stakeholder dynamics and aligning your message with individual needs.

The story of Tony securing a deal by getting there first demonstrates how early engagement with key stakeholders can shape the buying process and give you a competitive advantage.

The contrasting approaches of Penske and its competitor in a truck leasing deal highlight the importance of showing genuine interest, building relationships, and tailoring your solution to the specific needs of the stakeholders.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

How can you effectively identify and map the BASIC stakeholders in your deals?

What are some strategies for engaging with different types of stakeholders and building strong relationships?

How can you leverage the influence of amplifiers and coaches to increase win probability?

Supporting Points

Asking questions, conducting research, and observing stakeholder interactions can help you identify key players and understand their roles in the decision-making process.

Tailoring your communication style, addressing individual concerns, and demonstrating empathy can enhance rapport and build trust with different stakeholders.

By cultivating amplifiers and coaches, you can gain valuable insights, access key decision-makers, and create a network of internal advocates for your solution.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that focusing on multiple stakeholders can be time-consuming and distract from closing the deal.

Stakeholders might have conflicting interests, making it difficult to align your message and satisfy everyone's needs.

Relying too heavily on amplifiers and coaches might create a dependence on internal advocates and neglect the importance of building your own credibility.

Rebuttals

Investing time in understanding stakeholder dynamics can save you time and effort in the long run by preventing stalls and increasing win probability.

Negotiation and conflict resolution are essential skills for navigating complex deals with multiple stakeholders. By finding common ground and creating win-win solutions, you can address conflicting interests effectively.

While amplifiers and coaches can be valuable assets, building your own credibility and demonstrating your expertise are crucial for earning the trust of all stakeholders.

Discussion Topics

The challenges of managing stakeholder relationships in complex sales environments.

The ethical considerations of leveraging stakeholder influence.

The role of technology in mapping and managing stakeholder relationships.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

Understanding and mapping the BASIC stakeholders in a deal allows you to tailor your sales approach, build strong relationships, and influence the decision-making process.

By cultivating amplifiers and coaches, you gain valuable insights, access key decision-makers, and create a network of internal advocates for your solution.

A comprehensive understanding of stakeholder dynamics can significantly increase win probability and create a more predictable and sustainable path to closing.

Counterpoints

Focusing on multiple stakeholders can be overwhelming and time-consuming, potentially distracting salespeople from core sales activities.

Stakeholder relationships can be complex and unpredictable, making it difficult to manage expectations and align interests effectively.

Relying too heavily on internal advocates might create a dependence on others and neglect the importance of building your own credibility and influence.

Rebuttals

A strategic and organized approach to stakeholder mapping and management can streamline your efforts and make the process more efficient.

Developing strong communication, negotiation, and relationship-building skills can help you effectively navigate the complexities of stakeholder interactions.

While leveraging internal advocates can be beneficial, it's crucial to establish your own credibility, demonstrate your expertise, and build direct relationships with key stakeholders.

Decision Process

The often irrational, emotional, and nonlinear process through which each stakeholder in a deal makes commitments of time, emotion, and action.

Main Concepts

The decision process is where strategy, logic, and human emotions collide, making it a crucial area for UHPs to master.

Aligning the three processes of sales (sales process, buying process, and decision process) is critical for success.

Understanding the five questions stakeholders ask during the decision process ("Do I like you?", "Do you listen to me?", "Do you make me feel important?", "Do you get me and my problems?", "Do I trust and believe you?") allows salespeople to influence outcomes.

Social proof is a powerful tool for aligning decision-making among stakeholders.

Supporting Evidence

The chapter emphasizes that UHPs are masters at perceiving, controlling, managing, and influencing irrational human emotions. Average salespeople often mistake the buying process for the decision process, leading them to focus on organizational steps rather than the individual stakeholder's journey.

Critical Thinking Resources

Critical Thinking Questions

How can you influence a stakeholder's decision process without being manipulative?

What are some ways to leverage social proof to gain buy-in from multiple stakeholders?

How can you identify and address the emotional concerns that may be driving a stakeholder's resistance?

Supporting Points

Building strong emotional connections with stakeholders is crucial for influencing their decisions.

Presenting a united front with other stakeholders who support your solution can create a powerful sense of social proof.

Addressing both the logical and emotional aspects of the stakeholder's concerns can enhance your persuasiveness.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that attempting to influence the decision process is ethically questionable.

The decision process can be highly subjective and unpredictable, making it difficult to influence consistently.

Focusing too much on influencing individual stakeholders might neglect the overall organizational dynamics and decision-making structure.

Rebuttals

Influencing the decision process ethically involves providing value, building trust, and helping stakeholders make informed choices that are in their best interest.

While the decision process might be unpredictable, understanding common emotional drivers and leveraging influence techniques can increase your odds of success.

While organizational dynamics are important, influencing the decisions of individual stakeholders who ultimately hold the power to approve or reject a deal is crucial for closing.

Discussion Topics

The ethical considerations of influencing the decision-making process in sales.

The role of emotional intelligence in navigating the complexities of stakeholder decisions.

The strategies for building consensus and gaining buy-in from a diverse group of stakeholders.

Argument Builder

Supporting Points

By understanding the decision process, salespeople can proactively address concerns, build consensus, and create a smoother path to closing.

Leveraging social proof and human influence frameworks can help salespeople create a sense of momentum and make it easier for stakeholders to say yes.

Mastering the art of influencing the decision process requires a high level of Sales EQ and a deep understanding of human psychology.

Counterpoints

Some might argue that influencing the decision process is a manipulative tactic that undermines the prospect's autonomy.

Focusing too much on individual stakeholders might neglect the broader organizational context and political dynamics.

Attempting to influence the decision process might backfire if stakeholders perceive it as a lack of respect for their established procedures.

Rebuttals

Influencing the decision process ethically involves providing value, building trust, and helping stakeholders make informed choices that align with their needs and objectives.

While organizational context is important, understanding the motivations and concerns of individual stakeholders who hold decision-making power is crucial for success.

Transparency and open communication can help address any concerns stakeholders might have about your involvement in the decision process.

Practical Application 1: BASIC Stakeholder Mapping

Actionable Task 17.1: Build a Stakeholder Map for Each Opportunity

Steps:

For each deal in your pipeline, identify the individuals who play the roles of Buyers, Amplifiers, Seekers, Influencers, and Coaches (BASIC).

Determine their level of influence, their attitude towards your solution, and their key motivations.

Resources:

Stakeholder mapping templates

CRM software

Internal contacts

LinkedIn

Obstacles/Solutions:

Difficult to identify all stakeholders? Start with the most obvious ones and use your initial conversations to uncover other influencers.

Timeline:

Create your stakeholder map before your first formal meeting with the prospect, and update it as you gain more information.

Actionable Task 17.2: Develop a Tailored Engagement Strategy

Steps:

Create a personalized engagement plan for each key stakeholder, considering their communication style, motivations, and potential concerns.

Resources:

Stakeholder persona templates

Communication style assessments

Insights from your research

Obstacles/Solutions:

Stakeholders have conflicting interests? Focus on finding common ground, building consensus, and creating win-win solutions.

Timeline:

Develop your engagement strategy within one week of creating your stakeholder map.

Evaluation:

Success is measured by your ability to identify key stakeholders, understand their motivations, and build rapport with them. Look for signs of engagement, willingness to collaborate, and advocacy for your solution.

Additional Resources

"The Challenger Customer: Selling to the Hidden Influencer Who Can Multiply Your Results" by Brent Adamson and Matthew Dixon (book)

Articles and resources on stakeholder management and influence mapping.

Chapter 18: Decision Process

By addressing emotional drivers and aligning the sales approach with the decision-making process, salespeople can enhance their effectiveness in closing deals.

Knowledge is Power

Chapter 18: Decision Process - Understanding the Emotional Journey

Key Concept: The buying decision is an emotional journey, influenced by both logic and feelings.

Blount explores the often-irrational and emotional nature of the decision process. He stresses the importance of aligning the three processes of sales (sales process, buying process, and decision process) and understanding the five key questions stakeholders ask:

"Do I like you?"

"Do you listen to me?"

"Do you make me feel important?"

"Do you get me and my problems?"

"Do I trust and believe you?"

He also emphasizes the power of social proof in aligning decision-making.

Practical Application 1: Aligning with the Decision Process

Actionable Task 18.1: Identify Emotional Drivers

Steps: During your interactions with stakeholders, listen attentively for clues that reveal their underlying emotional needs, fears, and aspirations related to the decision.

Resources: Active listening skills, emotional intelligence resources, stakeholder research.

Obstacles/Solutions: If you encounter difficulty identifying emotional drivers, ask questions that explore their hopes, fears, and past experiences related to similar decisions.

Timeline: This should be done throughout the sales process, paying close attention to both verbal and nonverbal cues.

Actionable Task 18.2: Address Both Logic and Emotions

Steps: When presenting your solution, acknowledge and address both the logical and emotional aspects of the decision. Provide data and evidence to support your claims, but also connect with the stakeholder's feelings and aspirations.

Resources: Develop compelling stories, testimonials, and analogies that illustrate the emotional benefits of your solution.

Obstacles/Solutions: If a prospect seems overly focused on logic and data, find ways to connect your solution to their personal values, goals, or aspirations to engage their emotions.

Timeline: Incorporate this approach into your presentations, proposals, and all communication with stakeholders.

Evaluation:

Success is measured by the stakeholder's willingness to share their emotional concerns, a shift in the conversation from purely logical arguments to a more personal and relatable level, and a greater sense of trust and connection.

Additional Resources:

"Thinking, Fast and Slow" by Daniel Kahneman (book)

Articles on emotional intelligence, decision-making psychology, and persuasion.
