## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/agent-evaluation-trajectory-testing

Test the Trajectory, Not Just the Answer | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Test the Trajectory, Not Just the Answer

Agent evaluation should inspect the full path: retrieved evidence, tool choices, tool arguments, state changes, intermediate artifacts, final output, and business outcome.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Trajectory testing evaluates the sequence of agent actions: routing, retrieval, tool calls, state changes, intermediate artifacts, approvals, final output, and business outcome.

Why

A final answer can look correct while the agent used the wrong source, skipped a required tool, leaked data, or failed to follow approval policy. The path matters as much as the answer.

Framework

Practical rules

Score artifact quality, process quality, and final outcome separately.

Validate tool choices and tool arguments, not just text.

Use hidden black-box tests at stable interfaces.

Classify failures by cause: agent, spec, grader, data, or ambiguity.

Use trace-grounded judges when deterministic checks are insufficient.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A correct-looking answer hides unsafe tool use.

A benchmark checks only final text.

A failure is labeled bad output without finding the broken layer.

The judge lacks the trace needed to evaluate behavior.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Do tests inspect tool calls?

Are retrieval results included in evaluation?

Are failure paths tested?

Can the evaluator see state transitions?

Are hidden tests protected from tuning?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2604.20087v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2509.10769v2 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.17787v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI agent evaluation is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/agent-observability-traces

Agent Observability Starts With Traces | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Agent Observability Starts With Traces

Production agents need structured traces for inputs, routing, retrieval, tool calls, memory reads and writes, costs, errors, approvals, and final outputs.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Agent observability is the ability to inspect a run as structured operational data: inputs, decisions, retrievals, tool calls, state changes, memory operations, approvals, costs, errors, and outputs.

Why

Without traces, teams cannot tell whether a failure came from routing, retrieval, prompting, tool execution, memory, model choice, or evaluation. Observability turns agent behavior into evidence.

Framework

Practical rules

Log transition-level step traces.

Record retrieval queries, selected evidence, and rejected evidence.

Capture tool arguments, outputs, latency, cost, and errors.

Represent state changes as causal events.

Expose trace summaries for review and debugging.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Only the final answer is stored.

Tool outputs are detached from the decision that used them.

Cost spikes cannot be attributed to a stage.

A memory write changes future behavior without an audit trail.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Can a run be replayed?

Can reviewers see evidence and tool calls?

Are costs and latency broken down by stage?

Are approvals visible in the trace?

Can failure cause be classified?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.10165v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.14688v2 — supporting research reference

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI agent observability is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/agent-pr-review-checklist

AI Agent PR Review Checklist | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

AI Agent PR Review Checklist

Every PR that changes agent behavior should be reviewed for architecture, safety, routing, grounding, tools, memory, prompts, evaluation, separation of concerns, and debuggability.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

An agent PR review checklist is a production governance tool for changes that affect routing, prompts, tools, memory, retrieval, evaluation, cost, safety, or human oversight.

Why

Agent behavior can change through code, config, prompts, schemas, tools, models, retrieval, or memory. A checklist keeps reviewers from focusing only on visible UI or final text.

Framework

Practical rules

Review architecture and request flow first.

Check deterministic safety, routing, and retrieval gates.

Inspect tool contracts, memory writes, and prompt changes.

Require tests for behavior and failure paths.

Ask whether the change preserves the agent constitution.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Logic moves into prompt text without tests.

A route bypasses RAG for knowledge tasks.

A tool gains new side effects without approval.

Evaluation covers only happy paths.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Does the change preserve explicit flow?

Are unsafe inputs blocked in code?

Are grounded categories forced through retrieval?

Are relevant tests updated?

Would you trust this in production?

Sources

Research references

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/agent-regression-testing

Regression Testing for AI Agents | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Regression Testing for AI Agents

Every agent behavior change should be tested against visible and hidden cases, failure paths, tool contracts, safety gates, and outcome checks before release.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Agent regression testing verifies that changes to prompts, tools, routing, memory, retrieval, models, or evaluation logic do not break required behavior.

Why

Agent behavior can change through small edits that look harmless. A prompt tweak, retriever setting, or schema change can silently alter refusal behavior, citations, or tool calls.

Framework

Practical rules

Run deterministic hard gates before expensive judges.

Maintain visible tests for development and hidden tests for release checks.

Use fail-before/pass-after tests for reported issues.

Map impacted tests to changed files or workflow stages.

Cover infeasible and missing-data cases, not only happy paths.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A prompt fix breaks routing.

A test suite checks only successful cases.

The agent overfits visible benchmark examples.

A model upgrade changes behavior without comparison tests.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What behavior changed?

Which tests fail before and pass after the fix?

Are refusal and escalation paths covered?

Are tool arguments validated in tests?

Do existing regressions still pass?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.15976v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2406.12952v3 — supporting research reference

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/agent-retrieval-precision

Agent Retrieval Precision | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Agent Retrieval Precision

Good retrieval is not just vector search. Production agents should combine lexical and semantic search, filter by metadata and workflow stage, deduplicate results, and check whether evidence is sufficient before answering.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Retrieval precision is the ability to return evidence that matches the user intent, entity, workflow stage, access scope, and factual need. It is broader than vector similarity.

Why

A powerful model with weak retrieval still produces weak answers. Exact identifiers, policy clauses, dates, forms, and requirement labels often require lexical search and metadata filters in addition to embeddings.

Framework

Practical rules

Infer intent and metadata filters before ranking results.

Combine BM25 or full-text search with vector retrieval.

Deduplicate results and preserve source metadata.

Pack the highest-value evidence into a token budget.

Run a sufficiency check before generation.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The system retrieves semantically similar but wrong-stage context.

Exact contract IDs or form names are missed.

Too many snippets crowd out the decisive source.

The model fills evidence gaps with plausible language.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What filters apply before semantic ranking?

Does exact search work for IDs and names?

Is retrieved context deduplicated?

Can the system say evidence is insufficient?

Are source excerpts visible?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.02473v2 — primary research reference

arXiv:2601.10702v2 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2512.12818v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, agent retrieval precision is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/ai-agent-memory-state-design

Memory Is an Application Feature | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Memory Is an Application Feature

Agent memory should be explicit application state, not a vague extension of chat history. Durable memory needs schemas, source links, admission rules, retrieval filters, revision history, and audit logs.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Agent memory is a governed persistence layer for facts, episodes, decisions, preferences, traces, and workflow state. It should be represented as structured application data, not as an ever-growing chat transcript.

Why

Long-running agents need continuity, but unmanaged memory becomes a durable hallucination store. Good memory design preserves source evidence, supports correction, limits retrieval scope, and makes state changes auditable.

Framework

Practical rules

Store verbatim episodes before extracting summaries or facts.

Represent workflow state as typed schema-validated objects.

Attach source IDs and timestamps to every durable fact.

Use explicit ADD, UPDATE, DELETE, or NOOP memory operations.

Filter retrieval by identity, workflow stage, and evidence state.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A summary overwrites the original source.

The agent stores a user guess as a confirmed fact.

Conflicting memories are retrieved together without warning.

Memory from one customer or project appears in another context.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Where is canonical state stored?

Can each memory fact be traced to evidence?

Are writes logged as explicit operations?

How are conflicts resolved?

Can stale or rejected memories be excluded?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.27910v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2602.17902v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2508.19828v5 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI agent memory is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/approval-workflows-for-agents

Approval Workflows for AI Agents | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Approval Workflows for AI Agents

Consequential agent actions should become structured approval requests before they affect users, systems, money, data, or external commitments.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

An approval workflow converts a proposed agent action into a structured review state: pending, approved, rejected, revised, escalated, expired, or safely aborted.

Why

Agents can draft useful work, but external side effects need accountable authorization. Approval workflows separate proposing an action from executing it.

Framework

Practical rules

Represent proposed actions as structured intents.

Validate identity, scope, arguments, and risk before review.

Show reviewers the expected effect and alternatives.

Reauthorize if the plan or state changes.

Log approvals, rejections, waivers, and escalations.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The agent grants itself permission.

A stale approval is reused after the plan changes.

The reviewer cannot see the actual tool arguments.

A rejection produces an unbounded retry loop.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Is approval tied to a stable principal?

Are arguments and side effects visible?

Is approval scoped to current state?

Are waivers explicit?

Does rejection have a lifecycle?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.16708v2 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.26221v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2604.21910v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI approval workflows is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/cost-aware-model-routing

Cost-Aware Model Routing | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Cost-Aware Model Routing

Cost-aware agents should use the cheapest capable model for each stage, but escalate when confidence, grounding, risk, or verification fails.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Cost-aware model routing chooses the cheapest model or workflow path that is likely to meet the required quality, latency, risk, and evidence standard for the current stage.

Why

Using the strongest model for every step wastes money. Using the cheapest model for every step creates hidden quality failures. Routing makes the tradeoff explicit.

Framework

Practical rules

Estimate task risk and expected utility before model selection.

Use cheap-first paths for low-risk, well-grounded stages.

Escalate when retrieval is weak or verification fails.

Let safety, compliance, and customer commitments override cost.

Measure cost per successful validated task.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Simple extraction uses an expensive model by default.

High-risk compliance work stays on a cheap model.

The system tracks token spend but not success.

Retries repeat the same failing cheap path.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What stage is being routed?

What quality threshold applies?

What evidence triggers escalation?

How are cost and latency logged?

Does safety override routing?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.11931v2 — primary research reference

arXiv:2604.07494v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2604.16646v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, LLM cost optimization is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

Related guides

Continue the cluster

When To Use Bigger Model

Agent Observability Traces

Agent Regression Testing

FAQ

Common questions

What is LLM cost optimization?

Cost-aware agents should use the cheapest capable model for each stage, but escalate when confidence, grounding, risk, or verification fails.

Why does this matter for production agents?

Because reliable agents must be grounded, observable, testable, cost-aware, and reviewable before they affect business workflows.

How does URXION apply this?

URXION applies these patterns to RFP response, compliance review, SDR research, and custom AI workflow agents.

How URXION applies this

URXION uses evidence-first agent patterns in RFP response, compliance review, SDR research, and custom business workflows. The goal is review-ready work, not unsupervised automation.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/document-worker-agents

Document Worker Agents | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Document Worker Agents

For document-heavy workflows, assign each worker to a specific document or evidence bundle, restrict retrieval to that scope, and let the coordinator aggregate independent findings.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

A document worker is a specialized agent assigned to a specific document, attachment, or evidence bundle. Its job is to extract, cite, and validate facts from that assigned source.

Why

RFP and compliance workflows often involve many attachments. Document-scoped workers reduce cross-document contamination and make every extracted requirement traceable.

Framework

Practical rules

Assign one worker per important document or bundle.

Restrict each worker’s retrieval tools to its assigned scope.

Require citations for extracted requirements and evidence.

Cap searches before allowing an absence claim.

Let the coordinator aggregate findings into matrices and gap lists.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A worker cites the wrong attachment.

A missing requirement is assumed absent after one shallow search.

Evidence from one vendor file contaminates another review.

The final matrix lacks page or section references.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What document is each worker assigned?

Are citations specific enough for review?

How many searches are required before claiming absence?

How are duplicate findings merged?

Can the coordinator trace every row?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.08329v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2602.16901v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.14688v2 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, document AI agents is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/grounding-beats-guessing

Grounding Beats Guessing | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Grounding Beats Guessing

Knowledge-base agents should retrieve relevant source material before answering. If evidence is missing or weak, they should show the gap, retrieve again, ask for clarification, or abstain instead of guessing.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Grounding is the practice of connecting an agent output to retrieved, source-linked evidence. In a grounded workflow, the answer is constrained by documents, data, user-provided artifacts, or approved memory rather than by the model’s general training alone.

Why

Grounding matters whenever an answer affects an RFP, compliance review, customer claim, policy interpretation, or operational decision. If the system cannot find enough evidence, the right behavior is to show the gap, ask for more source material, or abstain.

Framework

Practical rules

Classify whether the user request requires evidence before generation.

Run retrieval before drafting for knowledge-base and document-grounded tasks.

Attach source IDs, excerpts, and evidence status to important claims.

Use sufficiency checks before answering from retrieved material.

Make retrieval failures visible instead of hiding them in confident prose.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The agent answers from model memory when the answer should come from the knowledge base.

Retrieved snippets are loosely related but not sufficient for the claim.

The output cites sources that do not support the sentence.

The user never sees that required evidence was missing.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Does this answer require source material?

What documents or records support each claim?

Is the retrieved evidence sufficient or only suggestive?

Are source links visible to the reviewer?

What happens when retrieval returns nothing useful?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.02704v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.02473v2 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.25097v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, RAG and grounded agents is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/human-in-the-loop-agent-design

Human-in-the-Loop Is Not a Checkbox | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Human-in-the-Loop Is Not a Checkbox

Human oversight should be designed into the workflow as explicit approval, escalation, rejection, and timeout states with enough evidence for accountable review.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Human-in-the-loop design places accountable people at consequential decision points while agents prepare evidence, drafts, options, risks, and recommended next actions.

Why

A vague review step becomes rubber-stamping. Real oversight requires structured context, authority boundaries, rejection paths, and timeout behavior.

Framework

Practical rules

Define which action classes require human approval.

Give reviewers concise narratives with evidence, risk, alternatives, and expected effect.

Bind approval to identity, scope, arguments, and current state.

Capture structured rejection reasons and bounded revision attempts.

Define escalation and safe fallback when humans are unavailable.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Chat consent is treated as authorization.

A reviewer receives a draft without evidence or risk notes.

Timed-out approvals become implicit yes.

The agent repeats a rejected action unchanged.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Who is authorized to approve?

What evidence does the reviewer see?

What happens after rejection?

What is the timeout path?

Can approvals be audited later?

Sources

Research references

arXiv:2601.15599v3 — primary research reference

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/llm-judge-calibration

LLM Judges Need Calibration | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

LLM Judges Need Calibration

LLM judges can help evaluate agents, but only when their prompts, schemas, reliability, bias, and disagreement rates are tested against human-labeled examples.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

LLM judge calibration is the process of testing whether evaluator models produce stable, rubric-aligned judgments under schema checks, perturbations, order swaps, and human comparison.

Why

Automated judges can be useful, but they can also be biased, unstable, or overly impressed by fluent answers. Calibration prevents judges from becoming unverified authority.

Framework

Practical rules

Use structured JSON outputs with explicit criteria.

Judge one criterion at a time for important rubrics.

Run pairwise comparisons with candidate order swapped.

Compare automated judges to a human-labeled panel.

Escalate high-disagreement cases.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The judge prefers longer answers regardless of accuracy.

Candidate order changes the winner.

Invalid judge JSON enters metrics.

The judge scores without seeing source evidence or trace data.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Is judge output schema-validated?

Has order bias been tested?

Is there human calibration data?

Are disagreements tracked?

Does the judge see enough evidence?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2508.17393v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.24586v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.14633v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, LLM judge calibration is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/minimum-viable-agent

The Minimum Viable Agent | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

The Minimum Viable Agent

A minimum viable agent should have explicit flow, tool authorization, schema validation, grounding for knowledge tasks, basic state, logging, tests, and human approval for high-impact actions before it gets more autonomy.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

A minimum viable agent is the smallest useful workflow that can complete one bounded task with explicit inputs, outputs, tools, validation, telemetry, and review gates. It is not a chatbot with many vague capabilities.

Why

Starting too broad creates brittle autonomy. A small governed workflow lets the team prove value, find failure modes, and add memory, tools, or delegation only when there is evidence that complexity is needed.

Framework

Practical rules

Choose one business workflow with a concrete output.

Define required inputs, forbidden actions, and completion criteria.

Use deterministic validation before and after the model call.

Add tool access only through explicit contracts.

Measure success, latency, cost, and review burden before expanding scope.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The agent is expected to handle every request in a domain.

No one defines what a successful output looks like.

Tool access is added before authorization policy.

Memory is added before the stateless workflow is stable.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What single workflow is this agent responsible for?

What inputs are required to proceed?

What should the agent refuse or escalate?

What tests prove the workflow works?

What must be true before adding autonomy?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.07379v1 — supporting research reference

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/multi-agent-orchestration

Multi-Agent Orchestration Without Chaos | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Multi-Agent Orchestration Without Chaos

Multi-agent systems need an orchestrator, not a free-for-all. Worker messages, state promotion, tool access, and completion signals should be mediated through explicit contracts.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Multi-agent orchestration is the coordination layer that assigns work, controls communication, mediates state, validates outputs, and decides when results can be promoted to the main workflow.

Why

Multiple agents can accelerate work, but uncoordinated workers create conflicting state, duplicate actions, hidden assumptions, and audit gaps. Orchestration makes parallel work governable.

Framework

Practical rules

Route worker communication through an orchestrator or broker.

Assign scoped responsibilities and tool permissions to each worker.

Use structured messages with sender, receiver, type, timestamp, and state references.

Require validation before worker output affects canonical state.

Keep planner, executor, and evaluator workspaces separate when independence matters.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Workers overwrite each other’s outputs.

An agent acts on stale or partial state.

A worker uses tools outside its assignment.

Evaluator and planner share private scratch work and lose independence.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Who owns canonical workflow state?

How are worker messages logged?

Can workers directly communicate or only through the hub?

What validates a worker result?

Who can promote results to production state?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2601.09883v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2509.21862v2 — supporting research reference

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/prompts-do-not-enforce-safety

Prompts Do Not Enforce Safety | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Prompts Do Not Enforce Safety

Prompts can guide model behavior, but they cannot reliably enforce authorization, privacy, tool policy, or high-risk workflow controls. Safety must be implemented in code at system boundaries.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Prompt safety means asking the model to behave safely. Runtime safety means the application enforces boundaries regardless of what the model writes. Production agents need runtime safety because prompts can be ignored, misinterpreted, or overridden by untrusted context.

Why

Documents, web pages, emails, tool outputs, and memory can all contain text that tries to steer the agent. If the application treats that text as authority, a model can leak data or trigger side effects even when the prompt says not to.

Framework

Practical rules

Run input classification and sanitization before the model sees untrusted content.

Treat retrieved documents and tool outputs as data, not instructions.

Validate every tool call against schema, identity, permission, and risk policy.

Filter outputs server-side before delivery to users, logs, or external tools.

Escalate high-impact or ambiguous actions to human review.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A retrieved document says to ignore system instructions.

A tool output asks the agent to send secrets elsewhere.

A prompt contains safety rules but no enforcement layer exists.

A model-generated tool argument includes private memory data.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What content is trusted instruction versus untrusted data?

Which safety rules are enforced in code?

Can the model bypass a forbidden action?

Are outputs filtered before external delivery?

Are risky actions reviewed before execution?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2503.12188v2 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.12277v4 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2604.23887v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI guardrails is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/rag-security-prompt-injection

RAG Security: Treat Context as Data | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

RAG Security: Treat Context as Data

Retrieved documents, web pages, emails, and tool outputs are untrusted data. They should not be allowed to create goals, override instructions, request secrets, or authorize actions.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

RAG security is the set of controls that prevent retrieved documents, web pages, tool outputs, or memory from becoming trusted instructions.

Why

Retrieval brings untrusted text into the agent context. That text can contain malicious or conflicting instructions that try to override user intent or system policy.

Framework

Practical rules

Tag every context chunk with origin and trust level.

Sanitize untrusted documents before prompt inclusion.

Ignore external instructions that conflict with trusted policy.

Run safety checks after retrieval as well as before.

Quarantine suspicious memory or retrieved content.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A document tells the agent to ignore prior instructions.

A retrieved page requests secrets or tool calls.

Tool output expands the task scope.

Untrusted content influences a side-effecting action.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Is retrieved content marked as data?

Can external text authorize actions?

Are suspicious chunks quarantined?

Does safety rerun after retrieval?

Are memory writes from untrusted content gated?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2601.17549v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2604.13630v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2601.17887v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, RAG security is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/source-linked-agent-memory

Source-Linked Memory Prevents False Memories | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Source-Linked Memory Prevents False Memories

Every durable memory fact should point back to its source. Without provenance, agents can preserve extraction errors, user mistakes, or stale assumptions as if they were truth.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Source-linked memory stores each semantic fact with a pointer to the episode, document, trace, or artifact that supports it. The source remains inspectable even after the fact is summarized or consolidated.

Why

Agents often need to remember preferences, decisions, constraints, and commitments. Without source links, a memory cannot be verified, challenged, rolled back, or safely promoted into future context.

Framework

Practical rules

Keep append-only raw logs or episodes as evidence.

Extract atomic facts separately from the raw source.

Assign evidence states such as candidate, accepted, rejected, stale, or disputed.

Retrieve prior related facts before writing a potentially conflicting update.

Quarantine suspicious or untrusted memories until reviewed.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

The agent remembers a preference the user never confirmed.

A corrected fact is overwritten by an older summary.

A hallucinated extraction becomes a durable memory.

A reviewer cannot find the original source of a stored claim.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Does every memory link to a source?

Is the source immutable or recoverable?

Are rejected facts excluded from normal retrieval?

Are revisions append-only?

Is there a rollback path?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2603.19935v1 — primary research reference

arXiv:2603.25097v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.17244v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, source-linked memory is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

Related guides

Continue the cluster

Ai Agent Memory State Design

Rag Security Prompt Injection

Agent Observability Traces

FAQ

Common questions

What is source-linked memory?

Every durable memory fact should point back to its source. Without provenance, agents can preserve extraction errors, user mistakes, or stale assumptions as if they were truth.

Why does this matter for production agents?

Because reliable agents must be grounded, observable, testable, cost-aware, and reviewable before they affect business workflows.

How does URXION apply this?

URXION applies these patterns to RFP response, compliance review, SDR research, and custom AI workflow agents.

How URXION applies this

URXION uses evidence-first agent patterns in RFP response, compliance review, SDR research, and custom business workflows. The goal is review-ready work, not unsupervised automation.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/system-not-the-model

The System Is Not the Model | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

The System Is Not the Model

A reliable AI agent is not just an LLM prompt. It is a governed application pipeline that routes intent, retrieves evidence, validates inputs, calls tools, logs state, evaluates outputs, and escalates when risk is too high.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

An AI agent architecture is the full software system around the model: request intake, routing, retrieval, policy checks, tool gateways, state, logging, evaluation, and human approval. The model generates or plans, but the surrounding application decides what is allowed, what evidence is required, and when work is complete.

Why

This matters because production failures are usually system failures rather than model failures. A prompt can sound careful while the application still allows hidden control flow, missing evidence, unsafe tool calls, or unreviewed side effects. Treating the system as the product makes the workflow inspectable and testable.

Framework

Practical rules

Draw the request path from intake to final approval before writing prompts.

Put routing, retrieval, tool authorization, and output checks in code rather than prompt prose.

Give the model a bounded role such as planner, extractor, drafter, or reviewer.

Log each state transition so failures can be traced to the right layer.

Define acceptance criteria before generation starts.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A prompt contains business policy that no test can inspect.

A tool call executes because the model asked for it, not because a policy gate approved it.

The final answer looks polished but cannot be traced to source evidence.

Debugging turns into prompt guessing because routing and state are hidden.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

Can a reviewer draw the agent flow as a pipeline or graph?

Can routing be tested without calling the LLM?

Does every external action pass through a gateway?

Are completion criteria explicit?

Can a failed run be replayed from logs?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.14281v3 — primary research reference

arXiv:2604.17240v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.20028v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI agent architecture is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/tool-use-governance

Tool Use Governance | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

Tool Use Governance

Agents should not call tools directly. Tool calls should pass through a trusted gateway that validates schema, identity, authorization, rate limits, risk, and audit requirements.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Tool use governance is the runtime layer that validates and authorizes agent tool calls before they reach real systems, APIs, files, messages, or databases.

Why

Tools turn generated text into action. Without a trusted gateway, a hallucinated or injected instruction can become a real side effect.

Framework

Practical rules

Route all tools through a central gateway.

Validate schema, required fields, allowed values, and policy constraints.

Attach actor, tenant, resource, and risk context to each call.

Expose only stage-appropriate least-privilege tools.

Treat tool outputs and metadata as untrusted data.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

A broad tool can perform many unintended actions.

The LLM bypasses authorization because it can call a server directly.

Tool metadata injects instructions into the model.

Malformed arguments reach production APIs.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What gateway sees every call?

What permissions does each tool require?

Are schemas strict?

Are mutating calls approval-gated?

Are tool outputs sanitized before reuse?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.14281v3 — primary research reference

arXiv:2512.23611v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2509.07595v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, AI tool governance is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

## /resources/ai-agent-engineering/when-to-use-bigger-model

When to Use a Bigger Model | URXION AI Agent Engineering

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

AI Agent Engineering

When to Use a Bigger Model

Use a bigger model when the expected cost of failure exceeds the incremental model cost, or when retrieval, safety, verification, or domain risk indicates the cheap path is unreliable.

Back to guide Custom agents

Def

Model escalation is a controlled decision to move from a cheaper model or workflow to a stronger one because risk, uncertainty, or validation failure justifies the additional cost.

Why

Bigger models should not be prestige defaults. They should be used when the cost of being wrong is meaningful or when the cheap path cannot meet evidence and quality requirements.

Framework

Practical rules

Compute risk before choosing a model.

Run cheap outputs through deterministic or judge-based validators.

Escalate on weak evidence, failed schemas, safety labels, or low confidence.

Bound retries and require new evidence for repeated attempts.

Log escalation reasons and downstream outcomes.

Failure modes

What goes wrong

Escalation happens only after a user complains.

A cheap model handles policy-sensitive work because the prompt is short.

The same failed call is retried with no changed context.

No one can explain why a bigger model was used.

Checklist

Implementation checklist

What failure would escalation prevent?

Is the task high-risk or evidence-sensitive?

Did verification fail?

Is the incremental cost justified?

Was the escalation reason logged?

Sources

Research references

These arXiv references are the source IDs used in URXION's internal agent constitution notes. Verify applicability before treating any research item as production policy.

arXiv:2602.19509v3 — primary research reference

arXiv:2504.07113v1 — supporting research reference

arXiv:2603.23013v1 — supporting research reference

Implementation example

How this looks in practice

In a URXION-style workflow, model escalation is treated as an operational design concern. The system records the input, identifies required evidence, routes the task through the right checks, and produces review-ready artifacts with visible gaps instead of pretending the output is final.

Implementation Plan: Mastering Managerial Accounting Concepts

This plan outlines actionable steps to grasp and implement key managerial accounting concepts from the provided lecture and text. It assumes no prior knowledge, building a solid foundation before tackling real-world applications.

Phase 1: Building Foundational Knowledge

Key Concept 1: Cost Behavior and Activity Cost Drivers

Explanation: Costs behave differently based on changes in activity levels (output). Understanding this behavior is crucial for predicting future costs.

Formula: Total Cost = Fixed Cost + (Variable Rate x Output)

Actionable Task 1.1: Identify Your Business's Cost Structure

Steps:

List all significant costs your business incurs (e.g., rent, salaries, materials, marketing).

Categorize each cost as Fixed, Variable, or Mixed.

For Mixed costs, estimate the fixed and variable components.

Resources:

Accounting records

Business expense reports

Industry benchmarks

Obstacles/Solutions:

Difficulty categorizing mixed costs: Research industry standards or seek expert advice.

Evaluation Criteria:

Successfully categorize 90% of costs and accurately estimate fixed/variable components for mixed costs.

Key Concept 2: Break-Even Analysis

Explanation: The break-even point is the level of sales where total revenue equals total costs (no profit or loss). This is essential for understanding profitability.

Formula: Break-Even Point (Units) = Fixed Costs / Contribution Margin per Unit

Contribution Margin per Unit = Selling Price per Unit - Variable Cost per Unit

Actionable Task 2.1: Calculate Your Business's Break-Even Point

Steps:

Gather data on fixed costs, selling price, and variable cost per unit.

Calculate the contribution margin per unit.

Determine the break-even point in units and sales revenue.

Resources:

Accounting records

Sales data

Cost estimation tools

Obstacles/Solutions:

Inaccurate cost estimates: Use multiple estimation techniques (high-low, scattergraph) or consider more advanced methods (regression analysis).

Evaluation Criteria:

Accurately calculate break-even point in both units and revenue.

Key Concept 3: Target Profit Analysis

Explanation: Determines the sales volume needed to achieve a specific profit goal.

Formula: Target Profit (Units) = (Fixed Costs + Target Profit) / Contribution Margin per Unit

Actionable Task 3.1: Set Profit Goals and Calculate Required Sales

Steps:

Set realistic short-term and long-term profit targets for your business.

Using the target profit formula, calculate the required sales volume (units and revenue) for each target.

Resources:

Same as for break-even analysis

Obstacles/Solutions:

Unrealistic profit targets: Re-evaluate goals based on market conditions and business capabilities.

Evaluation Criteria:

Set achievable profit goals and accurately calculate corresponding sales targets.

Additional Resources:

Introduction to Management Accounting textbooks (Horngren, Datar, Rajan is a good one)

Online courses on Coursera or edX

Phase 2: Applying Concepts to Decision Making

Key Concept 4: Relevant Costs

Explanation: Only future costs that differ among decision alternatives are relevant. Sunk costs are never relevant, and opportunity costs are always relevant.

Practical Application 1: Special Order Decision

Explanation: A customer offers to buy a large quantity at a discounted price. Should you accept?

Actionable Task 4.1: Analyze Special Order Profitability

Steps:

Identify incremental costs and revenues associated with the order (what changes if you accept?).

Consider opportunity costs if you have to sacrifice regular sales due to limited capacity.

Compare incremental revenues to incremental costs to determine profitability.

Resources:

Cost data

Sales forecasts

Capacity information

Obstacles/Solutions:

Difficulty estimating opportunity costs: Use market data or competitor analysis.

Evaluation Criteria:

Make a data-driven accept/reject decision based on relevant cost analysis.

Practical Application 2: Make or Buy Decision

Explanation: Should you produce a component in-house or buy it from a supplier?

Actionable Task 4.2: Compare Make vs. Buy Costs

Steps:

Identify all relevant costs for both options (including opportunity costs of using internal resources).

Use differential analysis to highlight cost differences.

Consider qualitative factors (quality control, supplier reliability).

Resources:

Cost data

Supplier quotes

Production capacity data

Obstacles/Solutions:

Incomplete cost information: Conduct a thorough cost analysis for both options.

Evaluation Criteria:

Choose the most cost-effective option based on quantitative and qualitative factors.

Additional Resources:

Articles and case studies on special order decisions and make-or-buy decisions

Consult with a cost accountant or financial analyst for guidance

Phase 3: Continuous Learning and Refinement (Ongoing)

Actionable Task 5.1: Track and Monitor Results

Steps:

Regularly track actual costs, sales, and profitability against your forecasts and breakeven analysis.

Analyze variances to identify areas for improvement in your cost management and pricing strategies.

Resources:

Accounting systems

Data analytics tools

Performance dashboards

Obstacles/Solutions:

Data collection challenges: Implement efficient data tracking processes and integrate with accounting systems.

Timeline:

Ongoing (monthly or quarterly reviews)

Evaluation Criteria:

Focus on continuous improvement in cost control, pricing accuracy, and overall profitability.

Business Assessment

Knowledge is Power

Step 1: Basic Business Information

Let's start with some fundamental information about your business. This will help us calculate your revenue and costs.

Price per Unit ($)
The price you charge for one unit of your product/service.

Variable Cost per Unit (excluding commissions, $)
The direct cost to produce or deliver one unit of your product/service.

AE Commission Rate (%)
The percentage of the sale price your Account Executives (AEs) receive as commission.

Commission per Meeting Booked by SDR ($)
The amount you pay SDRs for each qualified meeting they book.

Average Units Purchased per Order
The typical number of units a customer buys in a single order.

## /try-rfp

Try URXION RFP | Public demo

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

URXION RFP demo

Start with your company. Generate from real RFP source material.

This public demo first looks for real cached public opportunities with source links. If the public cache does not have enough detail, paste the actual RFP or solicitation text on the next page before generating the package.

1

Describe your company or use an example profile

2

Review real cached public listings

3

Paste the full RFP before generating if needed

Start demo

Tell URXION what your company does.

If you only type one word like construction, the match will be weak. Use an example profile below or add details like project type, certifications, insurance, location, team, and past work.

Email you@company.com

Company name Example Company

Use construction example Use IT example Use facility services example

Company info, past work, certifications, or capabilities
Find Real Cached RFPs

Important demo limits

No fake RFP opportunities.

Public opportunity matching uses cached real public listing snippets with source links.

Many official RFPs require login, attachments, or buyer portals to access full documents.

If no real cached listing is available, URXION asks you to paste a real RFP instead of showing fake opportunities.

You can paste the actual RFP on the next page, right before generating the package.

Production workflows use stronger models, full RFP packages, source files, evidence folders, and deeper review.

No demo output should be used as a final bid without human review.

## /why-urxion

Urxion | Built for My Own Bottlenecks
First

URXION
Products Resources Why URXION Demo Data & Security Book a call

Why Urxion

Built for My Own Bottlenecks First

I built Urxion's agents for my own business before offering them
to anyone else. These are not demos. They are the systems I use
to find work, qualify opportunities, win contracts, manage risk,
and turn messy business processes into repeatable workflows.

Book a free discovery call See URXION RFP

1

Read the work

2

Structure the evidence

3

Surface risk

4

Stop before human judgment

Founder conviction

I built these systems for myself first.

Not as demos. Not as AI theater. As operating infrastructure for
the problems I actually face as a founder: finding work,
qualifying opportunities, winning contracts, managing risk, and
turning messy business processes into repeatable workflows.

Most companies do not need another AI chatbot. They need systems
that can read the work, structure the evidence, surface the
risks, draft the next step, and stop before a human decision is
required.

That is the philosophy behind Urxion.

The human stays accountable. The system makes the human faster,
sharper, and less likely to miss what matters.

Operating rule

The rule every agent follows.

Do the heavy cognitive work.
Show the evidence.
Surface the risk.
Prepare the action.
Stop before the decision.

The operating philosophy

Evidence first. Fail closed. Human approved.

Evidence first

Every claim needs a source. If the system cannot support
something, it flags it instead of pretending.

Fail closed

Missing information stops the workflow. The agent does not
guess its way through a business-critical decision.

Human approval required

The system can research, extract, compare, draft, and
recommend. It does not submit, send, certify, or decide on
its own.

Built from lived operating pain

These were not built because AI is fashionable. They were
built because I needed leverage in my own business.

Augmentation, not replacement

The point is to remove administrative drag around the human
so judgment can happen faster and with better evidence.

The three systems

Different workflows. Same operating pattern.

URXION RFP: Finding and Winning AI Contracts

I built URXION RFP because I wanted to compete for AI and
technology contracts without needing a full proposal team.

Government and enterprise RFPs are hard because of the
hidden work around the writing: finding relevant
opportunities, reading dense procurement documents,
extracting requirements, mapping evidence, spotting gaps,
deciding whether to bid, and turning everything into a
credible proposal.

Why I built it:

Small expert firms
should not lose winnable contracts because they do not have
a proposal department.

URXION SDR: Finding the Right Clients Without Spam

I built URXION SDR because I needed a way to find clients
without becoming the kind of outbound machine everyone
ignores.

URXION SDR starts with research. It studies a target
account, looks for real business signals, connects those
signals to what I can actually deliver, and drafts short
outreach that sounds like a human with a reason to write.

Why I built it:

Good outbound should
feel like a useful observation, not an automated
interruption.

URXION Compliance: Catching Risk Before It Becomes Expensive

I built URXION Compliance because operational risk usually
shows up after someone should have checked the paperwork.

URXION Compliance reviews onboarding documents, extracts
evidence, maps it against requirements, and produces a
prioritized remediation plan.

Why I built it:

Compliance should not
depend on memory, inbox archaeology, or hoping someone
checked the expiry date.

The bigger thesis

What Urxion Really Builds

Urxion builds agentic workflows for business bottlenecks.

Not generic AI assistants. Not chatbots looking for a use case.

I look for the part of the operation where smart people are
slowed down by document review, evidence matching, repetitive
drafting, compliance checking, intake triage, or manual
coordination.

Then I build the workflow around that bottleneck.

Better inputs.
Clearer evidence.
Faster review.
Fewer missed risks.
More consistent execution.
Human approval at the point of judgment.

The common thread

Messy work becomes operating discipline.

These products look different on the surface: one helps win
contracts, one helps find clients, and one helps reduce
compliance risk.

But underneath, they are the same system pattern. They all turn
messy, document-heavy, judgment-heavy workflows into structured
operating systems.

Evidence first

Fail closed

Human approval required

Built from lived operating pain

Augmentation, not replacement

AI should not be a novelty layer on top of broken processes.

It should be the operating system that helps people do important
work with more speed, more evidence, and more control.

Book a free discovery call
